The positions are at the NOAA National Ocean Service Laboratory in Charleston, South Carolina and will involve a commitment of 20 hours per week extending over a 14 week period from September 9 to December 13, 2013. There is some flexibility in these start and end dates. \n \nInterns will primarily assist with laboratory activities such as data entry, photo-analysis, and stranding response, in addition to participating in a limited amount of fieldwork. Building on existing data from long-term monitoring which has spanned 15+ years, boat-based photo-identification (id) surveys will be conducted for Western North Atlantic bottlenose dolphins in estuaries and near-shore waters of South Carolina as well as remote biopsy surveys near Jacksonville, FL. Specific research questions focus on relationships between contaminants and environmental factors.  The internship offers an excellent opportunity for qualified and motivated individuals to obtain field and laboratory training in photo-id methodology and analysis under the mentorship of experienced dolphin researchers. \n \nThere is no compensation for this position, and interns will be responsible for their own living expenses and transportation to and from the laboratory. There may be travel involved for some components of the fieldwork, which will be paid for by the laboratory.\n \nIdeal applicants will be advanced undergraduates or\nrecent graduates of a scientifically-oriented university program in marine science, biology or a related field. \nPreference will be given to applicants with well-developed computer skills and boat-based field experience. The internship application consists of a letter of interest, transcripts of university coursework and two letters of recommendation from professors or research supervisors who are familiar with applicant\u2019s\nscholarship, research skills and work habits relevant to the internship. \n\nInterested applicants should first correspond with Todd Speakman by email (Todd.Speakman@noaa.gov) before\npreparing and submitting application materials. We anticipate filling this internship position by the August 15, 2013."}

Celebrating Black History with y'all !", "id": "10151448591579533_27237001", "user_likes": false}]}, "privacy": {"value": ""}, "actions": [{"link": "https://www.facebook.com/32963389532/posts/10151448591579533", "name": "Comment"}, {"link": "https://www.facebook.com/32963389532/posts/10151448591579533", "name": "Like"}], "updated_time": "2013-02-05T17:52:49+0000", "shares": {"count": 3}, "created_time": "2013-02-05T16:41:51+0000", "message": "We are blessed to have a blending of many cultures here in the United States and what we find over time is many of the cultures add their own flavor to the \"stew\" that is American culture.  Hispanic, African American, Jamaican, Chinese, Irish, German, and many other cultures have brought their own influences to the point where sometimes the influence can become so prevalent in day to day culture; many people often do not even realize where the influence originally came from. Food is a huge part of that.  As a result, many institutions, particularly educational institutions, try to celebrate and point out the influences so people appreciate these cultures and their contributions to our society.\n\nSoul food is one example of that.  There were many dishes that were developed by the slaves and introduced to the Americas as a result of the trans-Atlantic slave trade.  In addition many other dietary staples were developed by the slaves who were fed by their captors as cheaply and little as possible.  As a result, you often see menu items that utilize typically discarded meat (like pig's feet, oxtail, and ham hocks), used lard, cornmeal, and offal (like hushpuppies and deep fried foods) to bolster the filling, and supplemental items that could be found in small gardens (like collard greens, watermelons, wild garden items, etc.). These menu items, which started as a necessity, developed over time as families put their own spin and added their own flavoring.  Now soul food is a vital part of American cuisine that is celebrated around the world.  You can find restaurants around the world, and even here in Galveston, that specialize in soul food and African American cuisine.  We feel it is important to celebrate its origins and recognize the culture that brought us this fine food.  Our menu for Black History month was developed for this reason and was developed in conjunction with many of our staff who see this food as a point of pride.  It is also shared with the Office of Multicultural Education and Diversity in Student Life to ensure it fits as part of the educational program of Black History Month.\n\nDining Services will be Celebrating Black History Month with a Special Lunch\nWednesday February 6, 2013\n\nMenu:\nVegetable Gumbo Soup\nDeep Fried Catfish\nBaked Chicken\nPork Ribs\nMacaroni & Cheese\nHushpuppies\nBlack Eyed Peas\nChopped Collard Greens\nBean and Shell Pasta Salad\nHarvest Bar: African\nCherry Pie", "type": "status", "id": "32963389532_10151448591579533", "status_type": "mobile_status_update", "likes": {"paging": {"cursors": {"after": "NzAwOTE1NDg4", "before": "MTQxMjA5MzM4OQ=="}}, "data": [{"id": "1412093389", "name": "Ann Mueller Parsons"}, {"id": "757335137", "name": "SC Moore"}, {"id": "1423234110", "name": "Nancy Hansen"}, {"id": "1821950086", "name": "Nathan Durham"}, {"id": "838924061", "name": "Shannan Wolfe Rios"}, {"id": "1063656086", "name": "Pat McGuigan"}, {"id": "699948473", "name": "Lee Anne Wilde"}, {"id": "100001235779069", "name": "Constance Van Zandt"}, {"id": "574495413", "name": "Alicia Martin"}, {"id": "1512530815", "name": "Elizabeth Cortez"}, {"id": "549897497", "name": "Kathy Hunter Thurman"}, {"id": "100002251724033", "name": "CM Bailey"}, {"id": "1099865068", "name": "C Michael Bailey"}, {"id": "100000359906928", "name": "Michael Bailey"}, {"id": "100001341692220", "name": "Anne Marie Sarutto"}, {"id": "1041371027", "name": "Carolina Burgos"}, {"id": "1462914815", "name": "Martha Clark"}, {"id": "100000824553767", "name": "Sherry S. up to $760 for mileage/expense reimbursement \nHours:  The position is a 40-hour work week that requires working some weekends and holidays.  \nJob Description:  The intern\u2019s duties in the first half of the season will focus on sanctuary management and public education duties associated with the famed High Island spring bird migration.  The intern will work at several of Houston Audubon\u2019s 17 sanctuaries in the Houston area.  \nStarting in April, the intern\u2019s primary duties will include identifying, posting, maintaining, and monitoring nesting locations at Bolivar Flats (Least Terns & Wilson\u2019s Plovers) and the Texas City dike (Black Skimmers).  Shorebird surveys will be conducted every 7-10 days while nest monitoring will occur at Bolivar Flats 2-3 times per week, time allowing.\nThe intern will continue to perform public outreach and education duties throughout the entire season, offering information about migratory birds, providing interpretation at the Smith Oaks Sanctuary rookery, and beach-nesting birds (Texas City and Bolivar Flats).  The intern will also assist American Bird Conservancy throughout the season in conducting public awareness surveys about beach-nesting birds during stewardship activities carried out at Bolivar Flats and/or the Texas City dike.\nThe intern will be required to assist Houston Audubon in preparing interim and final reports submitted to American Bird Conservancy to meet the grant requirements that partially fund this position.  \nOther duties as assigned by Houston Audubon.\nQualifications:  The applicant should be working toward or have completed a bachelor\u2019s degree in Biology, Natural Resources, or Wildlife Sciences; be very interested in bird research and conservation; and be comfortable working with the general public to teach them about a suite of coastal migratory and nesting birds. Familiarity with hand tools is preferred. Experience with identifying, surveying, and monitoring shorebirds is strongly preferred.  A significant portion of time will be spent viewing birds through a binocular and spotting scope on Gulf beaches and nearby nesting areas.   Applicant must be comfortable communicating and working with recreational beach users, volunteers, community members. Strong verbal communication skills are a must. Spanish proficiency is a plus. \nBasic Microsoft Word and Excel skills are required. Valid driver's license and reliable personal vehicle are required for occasional travel between work sites (mileage/expense allotment of $760 at federal rate of .565 cents per mile). The individual will have the option to reside full or part time at the Houston Audubon dormitory in High Island, TX. This facility is rustic with bathroom, shower, microwave and refrigerator. Weather conditions vary and may include cold, strong winds, rain and storms, heat, and high humidity \u2013 biting insects will be prevalent throughout the season.   The best candidates will be able to thrive in these work conditions.\nApplication Instructions:  Send cover letter, resume or CV, 3 references, unofficial transcript, and letter of recommendation to: Richard Gibbons at rgibbons@houstonaudubon.org"}

This is an annual competition of ROTC and Merchant Marine Cadets from throughout the nation.  Typical competitors include the United States Naval Academy, United States Military Academy, United States Air Force Academy, Norwich University, Virginia Tech University, The Citadel, The United States Merchant Marine Academy, and numerous universities from across the nation. \r\n\r\nThis is not an easy competition, as each team\u2019s performance is graded by the watchful eyes of Marine Corps evaluators who know all the details of marching, facing movements, ceremonial display of rifles, and proper presentation of our nation\u2019s flag. Our team members have worked hard since the beginning of the fall 2012 semester so they can feel the pride associated with presenting our nation\u2019s flag with honor and dignity as well as marching with crispness, and precision, and a desire for overall excellence.  They have also developed their roles as team members.  Whether our cadet members are upper classmen in leadership roles, or underclassmen eagerly learning from experienced  seniors, juniors, and sophomores, each member has matured in ways that will benefit them down the road, whether in the classroom, the boardroom, on board a waterborne vessel, or in any other place of employment. If you see our team members, be sure to wish them well, as they will be our university\u2019s ambassadors at this grueling competition. \r\n\r\nTuesday February 12 (Fat Tuesday)\r\n\r\nThe Drill Team, Color Guard, and Honor Guard, as guests of the Mystic Krewe of Aquarius, will again lead this year\u2019s Fat Tuesday Parade on the Strand in Galveston.  The parade is scheduled to kick off at 6:30 P.M. at the Corner of 25th Street and Santa Fe Place Street, proceed through the streets of downtown and end where it started.
